### **Research question:**
Explore the feasibility of locating a supermarket at the intersection of Chalk Farm Road and Ferdinand Street, which is aim to cover the need of Camden neighborhood.


```python
#import the library
import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import matplotlib
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
import osmnx as ox # this line imports osmnx
import networkx as nx # this line imports networkx
import matplotlib.cm as cm
import matplotlib.colors as colors
```

### Introduction to Camden Community
**Camden** is situated in the northern part of central London and is renowned for its vibrant atmosphere, diverse markets, eclectic dining establishments, music venues, and lively street art. This community is not only one of London's most popular tourist destinations but also a residential area with a diverse population and a dynamic business environment. At its heart lies Camden Town, centered around Camden Market, attracting tourists and local residents alike from all over the world.

### Dataset Description
The dataset primarily originate from **OpenStreetMap (OSM)**  and is retrieved using the OSMnx library. OSM is a collaborative project aimed at creating a free, editable map of the world. With OSMnx, we can extract street network data for the Camden community, including information on roads, sidewalks, bike paths, and more.


```python
G=ox.graph_from_address('Camden,London',dist= 2000,network_type='drive')
#ox.plot_graph(G)
```


```python
G.nodes(data=True)
```

```python
edge = nx.to_pandas_edgelist(G)

filtered_edge = edge[edge['name'].str.contains('Chalk Farm Road', case=False, na=False)]

stats = ox.basic_stats(G)
```

### Closeness centrality
Closeness centrality considers how efficiently a node can reach all other nodes in the network. In our analysis, the assumed supermarket should be placed in the high closeness centrality area to make convenience for residents. 


```python
# some of the centrality measures are not implemented on multiGraph so first set as diGraph
DG = ox.get_digraph(G)
```


```python
# let's calculate edge closeness centrality: convert graph to a line graph so edges become nodes and vice versa
edge_cc = nx.closeness_centrality(nx.line_graph(DG))
```


```python
# set or inscribe the centrality measure of each node as an edge attribute of the graph network object
nx.set_edge_attributes(DG,edge_cc,'cc')
G1 = nx.MultiGraph(DG)
```


```python
nc = ox.plot.get_edge_colors_by_attr(G1, 'cc', cmap='plasma')
fig, ax = ox.plot_graph(G1, node_size=0, node_color='w', node_edgecolor='gray', node_zorder=2,
                        edge_color=nc, edge_linewidth=1.0, edge_alpha=1)
```


    
![png](Untitled_files/Untitled_13_0.png)
    


The varying colors represent different levels of centrality, with lighter colors (yellows) denoting higher centrality and darker colors oranges and (purples) indicating lower centrality. The lightest part is Belsize Park whcih is a residential area. Though our supermarket is not in the highest closeness centrality area, it is in orange and near the residential area, which still shows relevantly high centrality. 

### Shortest path

Though we have analyzed how convenient the transportation is around our picked place, it cannot represent for residents who choose public transportation to the supermarket due to the distribution of bus/underground stations. 

Since the Camden neighbourhood is run through by the northen line and overground line, what we need to consider is the distance from the nearest underground and overground station. 

Also, our assumed supermarket is only few metres away from the Chalk Farm underground station, therefore, we only need to consider the path between the supermarket and the neareast overground station, which is Kentish Town West. 


```python
# define origin/desination points then get the nodes nearest to each
origin_point = [51.5468426, -0.1466145] #The nearest overground station, Kentish Town West
destination_point = [51.5429011, -0.1493903] #Our aimed supermarket
origin_node = ox.nearest_nodes(G, origin_point[1],origin_point[0])
destination_node = ox.nearest_nodes(G, destination_point[1],destination_point[0])
origin_node, destination_node 

# find the shortest path between origin and destination nodes
route = nx.shortest_path(G, origin_node, destination_node, weight='length')
str(route)

# plot the route showing origin/destination lat-long points in red
#fig,ax = ox.plot_graph_route(G, route)

# Convert the graph G to GeoDataFrames
#gdf_nodes, gdf_edges = ox.graph_to_gdfs(G)
```




    '[25588462, 25588449, 25588455, 9998807446, 7799567407, 25596043, 109202, 434342969, 662643208, 454218635]'




```python
shortest_path = G.subgraph((route))
gdf_nodes, gdf_edges = ox.graph_to_gdfs(shortest_path)
Base_map = gdf_edges.explore(color='red')
Base_map
```

        function geo_json_e1094159d44da3ada7da7919a1aebb6f_pointToLayer(feature, latlng) {

                        e.target.setStyle(highlightStyle);
                    }
                },
            });
        };

    geo_json_e1094159d44da3ada7da7919a1aebb6f.bindTooltip(
    function(layer){
    let div = L.DomUtil.create(&#x27;div&#x27;);

    let handleObject = feature=&gt;typeof(feature)==&#x27;object&#x27; ? JSON.stringify(feature) : feature;
    let fields = [&quot;osmid&quot;, &quot;name&quot;, &quot;highway&quot;, &quot;maxspeed&quot;, &quot;oneway&quot;, &quot;reversed&quot;, &quot;length&quot;, &quot;ref&quot;, &quot;lanes&quot;];
    let aliases = [&quot;osmid&quot;, &quot;name&quot;, &quot;highway&quot;, &quot;maxspeed&quot;, &quot;oneway&quot;, &quot;reversed&quot;, &quot;length&quot;, &quot;ref&quot;, &quot;lanes&quot;];
    let table = &#x27;&lt;table&gt;&#x27; +
        String(
        fields.map(
        (v,i)=&gt;
        `&lt;tr&gt;
            &lt;th&gt;${aliases[i]}&lt;/th&gt;

            &lt;td&gt;${handleObject(layer.feature.properties[v])}&lt;/td&gt;
        &lt;/tr&gt;`).join(&#x27;&#x27;))
    +&#x27;&lt;/table&gt;&#x27;;
    div.innerHTML=table;

    return div
    }
    ,{&quot;className&quot;: &quot;foliumtooltip&quot;, &quot;sticky&quot;: true});


            geo_json_e1094159d44da3ada7da7919a1aebb6f.addTo(map_25295f6ff09b032acd02e40038718d08);

As shown in the graph, the red segments are the shortest path from the overground station to out assumed supermarket. Actually, from the Google map, it only takes 9 mins walk, which is an acceptable walking distance for people. 

To conclude, from our analysis, our selected place is thereotically ideal for locating a supermarket due to the high centrality and convenient transportation.
